<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dca22d98-16ae-46b1-9146-b18345945481'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer3281890840451729947">In a heartbreaking parting, a man gives his wife and daughter a last kiss and boards a steamship to cross the ocean. He's embarking on the most painful yet important journey of his life- he's leaving home to build a better future for his family.<br/><br/>Shaun Tan evokes universal aspects of an immigrant's experience through a singular work of the imagination. He does so using brill</span>
  <span id="freeText3281890840451729947" style="display:none">In a heartbreaking parting, a man gives his wife and daughter a last kiss and boards a steamship to cross the ocean. He's embarking on the most painful yet important journey of his life- he's leaving home to build a better future for his family.<br /><br />Shaun Tan evokes universal aspects of an immigrant's experience through a singular work of the imagination. He does so using brilliantly clear and mesmerizing images. Because the main character can't communicate in words, the book forgoes them too. But while the reader experiences the main character's isolation, he also shares his ultimate joy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3281890840451729947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/788188-the-people-could-form-relationships-so">The people could form relationships so well through the creatures everyone had. Do they mean to represent something?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_788188'><a id="like_count_community_question_788188" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/788188?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F920607.The_Arrival">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/788188-the-people-could-form-relationships-so">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/788188-the-people-could-form-relationships-so">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/99050534-mustafa-kemal"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/99050534-mustafa-kemal">Mustafa Kemal</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think it's about how there's a universal language. Instead of their pets being simply an allegory that represents something that we, the reader woul<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think it's about how there's a universal language. Instead of their pets being simply an allegory that represents something that we, the reader would relate to, they're a part of the universal language that EVERYBODY relates to. When you see two pets who can't communicate in human means feel mutual things, it makes you understand how people who can't communicate in human ways (i.e languages) can understand each other clearly. <br /><br />Pets, food, architecture, fashion, economy.. Everything complements this constant state of not "knowing" but "relating" or maybe even "recalling", in a vague way. For example when one of the natives we get to meet recalls a certain event (the invasion? War? idk man) to feel the main character.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/57099123-raphi">Raphi</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes, most definitely! Everything about it is gorgeous, and the storytelling is simply magnificent. There's also the added bonus that it will take you <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes, most definitely! Everything about it is gorgeous, and the storytelling is simply magnificent. There's also the added bonus that it will take you as long as you want it to to finish it, since it consists simply of pictures, though I do advise that you take your time with it and go through it slowly to get the most out of the images.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_1114070849" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114070849" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1114070849?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cristina Monica by: </span>
      Ana
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=real-life-matters">real-life-matters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114070849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7837390139629371151">There were no words in this graphic novel. No dialogs. No written sentences. No words. <br/><br/>But, as I realized throughout my read, they weren’t needed. The mesmerizing art was enough. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416805281i/12070259._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='500' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>And what illustrations! Never have I read such a graphic novel before!<br/><br/>It was a fast-read. I don’t think I’ve even spend thirty minutes to get through it. The story was poignant and I loved how realistically it portrayed immigrants and how metaphorically and fantastically the author drew the world-building and settings.</span>
  <span id="freeText7837390139629371151" style="display:none">There were no words in this graphic novel. No dialogs. No written sentences. No words. <br><br>But, as I realized throughout my read, they weren’t needed. The mesmerizing art was enough. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416805281i/12070259._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And what illustrations! Never have I read such a graphic novel before!<br><br>It was a fast-read. I don’t think I’ve even spend thirty minutes to get through it. The story was poignant and I loved how realistically it portrayed immigrants and how metaphorically and fantastically the author drew the world-building and settings.<br><br>It didn’t actually speak to me to an obvious point, as I maybe predicted, since, even though I am an emigrant too (Romania -&gt; Canada), I was very young at that time and we had someone to help us, unlike the main character who had to find help and shelter by himself. Still, I can perfectly understand the main character’s – untold – feelings and relate, in a way, to him. I was just probably more excited than he was and not as confused/lost.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416805281i/12070260._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aside for the graphics and settings, what I loved most was the fact that, not only we could see the main character’s experience at traveling and changing completely of surrounding, but also the people that he meets in his way and that give him some support. It was breathtakingly captivating.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416805281i/12070261._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I do have a complaint though: it was, like I said, too short. Too fast-paced. It could have been longer I believe, because every scene lasted less than two minutes or so. That did give some unrealism to the story – not including the settings which I like to consider well-fitting everything. It would also have been interesting to get to know his wife and child better, with some more scenes including them and maybe a little more to why he decided to leave his country. The blurb does implicitly or explicitly tell us why, depending on your point of view, but actually seeing it would have given some even more intensity to the story and a solid background. Although, I do understand that this is mainly about adaptation, experiences and going forward.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416805281i/12070262._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Absolutely recommended! Not only will it appear spectacular and surprising, to lovers of graphic novels or not, but it is also short and easy to get into the story. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7837390139629371151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5756209816122619466">To see this and other wordless picture book reviews, please visit <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.readrantrockandroll.com'>www.readrantrockandroll.com</a><br/><br/><i>The Arrival </i> by Shaun Tan is a graphic novel and wordless story of illustrations highlighting an immigrant man's journey told through an imaginary world.<br/><br/>I picked this up for my students a few years ago after hearing a special on NPR about it. We enjoyed following along in the story as the illustrations send powerful messages and emotions. It almost feels like a movie as you're turning the pages. <br/><br/>This is </span>
  <span id="freeText5756209816122619466" style="display:none">To see this and other wordless picture book reviews, please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readrantrockandroll.com">www.readrantrockandroll.com</a><br /><br /><i>The Arrival </i> by Shaun Tan is a graphic novel and wordless story of illustrations highlighting an immigrant man's journey told through an imaginary world.<br /><br />I picked this up for my students a few years ago after hearing a special on NPR about it. We enjoyed following along in the story as the illustrations send powerful messages and emotions. It almost feels like a movie as you're turning the pages. <br /><br />This is a great eye-opening and thought-provoking story that will help children and adults think about immigration including the fears and difficulties that come along with being alone in a strange place. <br /><br />5*****</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mutasim by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/43309961-tukunjil-nayeera">Tukunjil Nayeera</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2464005408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17993703557289469581">First of all, special thanks to Tukunjil Nayeera for recommending me this wonderful book.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532365118i/26017789.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>The Arrival</i> is a wordless graphic-novel that tells the tale of an immigrant father who leaves his family to work in a foreign land. The story is told in the form of sequential art with the mood being set with varying degrees of sepia-tone colored illustrations in multiple frames and panels. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532365746i/26017829._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The story takes place in a strange fantasy realm, where the hero immigrates to a different place to support his family.</span>
  <span id="freeText17993703557289469581" style="display:none">First of all, special thanks to Tukunjil Nayeera for recommending me this wonderful book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532365118i/26017789.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>The Arrival</i> is a wordless graphic-novel that tells the tale of an immigrant father who leaves his family to work in a foreign land. The story is told in the form of sequential art with the mood being set with varying degrees of sepia-tone colored illustrations in multiple frames and panels. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532365746i/26017829._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story takes place in a strange fantasy realm, where the hero immigrates to a different place to support his family. The struggles of the immigrant is showcased just using art and wordless storytelling. The purpose of the novel is to generate empathy among readers for the immigrants and refugees who have been frowned-upon in a world ruled by bigotry, by giving the readers a glimpse of the bigger picture.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532366081i/26017860._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Shaun Tan sets the mood of each scene with sepia-tone color schemes, ranging from grayscale to bright gold. The illustrations are reminiscent of aged photos(daguerreotypes), and often feature realistic-looking humans in abstract and bizarre environments. The environments resemble a combination of futuristic and old-fashioned aesthetics. Tan's process was one that used real-life models to create a storyboard. He also shot pictures in his garage, using a video camera and empty boxes to create lighting.<br><br>Highly recommended for readers of all ages.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532366081i/26017861._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10647158487767308693">This book is magnificent!<br/><br/>A wordless graphic novel that the tells the familiar tale of an immigrant, and somehow makes the story new and exciting.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469858493i/19864850._SY540_.png' width='400' height='550' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A man says goodbye to his wife and daughter, and sets out, taking only a suitcase containing a precious photograph of his family. He leaves a dark and ominous city for a journey across the sea. Days pass, each depicted by a drawing of the sky. The ship enters the harbor and a strange new world is revealed. The man is examined, cataloged, and labeled. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText10647158487767308693" style="display:none">This book is magnificent!<br><br>A wordless graphic novel that the tells the familiar tale of an immigrant, and somehow makes the story new and exciting.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469858493i/19864850._SY540_.png" width="400" height="550" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A man says goodbye to his wife and daughter, and sets out, taking only a suitcase containing a precious photograph of his family. He leaves a dark and ominous city for a journey across the sea. Days pass, each depicted by a drawing of the sky. The ship enters the harbor and a strange new world is revealed. The man is examined, cataloged, and labeled. Then he ventures forth into an amazing city. He is bombarded by new sights and sounds. Everywhere he looks, there is something he's never seen before. Even the food here is strange! He doesn't speak the language and must draw pictures of what he needs. He locates a place to stay and discovers an odd little roommate. He finds work and meets other immigrants who tell sad, horrifying stories of fear and oppression. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488973308i/22173162._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The monochromatic drawings are beautifully rendered in a style similar to Chris Van Allsburg, though I was reminded just a bit of M.C. Escher as well.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462505260i/19005842._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Adults will appreciate the simple story of a stranger in a foreign land, while children will be enraptured by the amazing drawings of fantastical creatures that populate this magical world.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488973748i/22173261.jpg" width="400" height="406" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is just a wonderful book to be looked at again and again, and a powerful reminder that we are all immigrants here.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488973443i/22173184._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3484014749058354859">This is a wondrous and wonderful book. Entirely told in drawings & pictures, not a word at all in the pages, apart from the title on the cover. My first 'graphic novel'. Beautifully designed 'in sepia', a weird and touching story. About a man who leaves his wife and little daughter to emigrate to a new country, to find work and earn a living. But it is no ordinary story, it is full of fantasy images, creatures and weird observations. It seems to be symbolic for people going to another country to</span>
  <span id="freeText3484014749058354859" style="display:none">This is a wondrous and wonderful book. Entirely told in drawings &amp; pictures, not a word at all in the pages, apart from the title on the cover. My first 'graphic novel'. Beautifully designed 'in sepia', a weird and touching story. About a man who leaves his wife and little daughter to emigrate to a new country, to find work and earn a living. But it is no ordinary story, it is full of fantasy images, creatures and weird observations. It seems to be symbolic for people going to another country to live, overcome by weird, scary but also beautiful new experiences. This is translated into a surrealistic, also scifi surrounding with the weirdest animals, shapes and creatures, scary experiences and wonderful encounters. A special book....highly recommended.</span>

<div id="review_405781739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/405781739" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/405781739?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=gn-silent">gn-silent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=eng-305-sum-16">eng-305-sum-16</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=gn-ya">gn-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=picturebooks-wordless">picturebooks-wordless</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=best-graphic-lit-ever">best-graphic-lit-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=gn-course-sum-18">gn-course-sum-18</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer405781739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16965696222531177748">6/19/18: Reading for summer YA GN and Comics class, wordless, a masterpiece everyone should own. Here I borrow from Agne's background on how Tan wrote it:<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.shauntan.net/books/the-arrival.html#anchor'>http://www.shauntan.net/books/the-arr...</a><br/><br/>The feel is silent movies, De Sica's (1948) The Bicycle Thief and photographs of immigrants on display at Ellis Island. Why is this book constantly timely in this country and in too many countries on the nature of refugees and immigrants. The separation of a parent from his child in this book is wrenching</span>
  <span id="freeText16965696222531177748" style="display:none">6/19/18: Reading for summer YA GN and Comics class, wordless, a masterpiece everyone should own. Here I borrow from Agne's background on how Tan wrote it:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.shauntan.net/books/the-arrival.html#anchor">http://www.shauntan.net/books/the-arr...</a><br /><br />The feel is silent movies, De Sica's (1948) The Bicycle Thief and photographs of immigrants on display at Ellis Island. Why is this book constantly timely in this country and in too many countries on the nature of refugees and immigrants. The separation of a parent from his child in this book is wrenching, especially in the light of camps for "tender age" children in this, my country.<br /><br />Original review, 6/19/16: The Arrival is Shaun Tan's masterpiece, a completely silent tale for all ages. A wordless book--except the title--it's about immigration and the wonder and largely dark strangeness and anxiety of that passage. In the U.S. the present conservative outcry about immigration is one that has lasted for at least 150 years here. "Give us your tired, your poor, your hungry . . . . " well, that Statue of Liberty was built in different times, eh? The concerns expressed by residents (and not just here in the U.S., of course) include such sentiments as "what does this have to do with us?" and "it's not my problem." Of course there is also a lot of generous sentiment for helping out people in need, as is also demonstrated across the world and will have to continue to be demonstrated for a long time.<br /><br />This book is dedicated to Tan's parents, who were once immigrants themselves.<br /><br />Steve Earle's Immigrant song: <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=75H8J6lURZc">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=75H8J...</a><br /><br />This book sets aside the politics, mostly, and focuses on the psycho-socio effects of immigrating, the strangeness, the anxiety, the fear, evidenced brilliantly by Tan in sepia-toned and darker shadings, and (especially) the creation of small and large fantastical creatures the immigrants face, symbolic of the newness and strangeness. Are the creatures cute? Are they scary? Depends on your perspective, in part. Maybe both welcoming and frightening.<br /><br />The focus of the story is on a small family who are separated as father goes ahead to the new country ahead of his wife and daughter. They must leave a place with dragons (and possibly other magical creatures) and come to a place of creatures of another kind. Language, customs, everything is foreign to him, but in time he makes friends, makes connections. Metaphor, allegory, are at the heart of this tale. Monsters are very real as we move to a new place. Maybe they can be conquered; maybe not. A paper bird made by father to make his sad daughter smile transfigures, emerges as something else, and again and again woven throughout. Magical, fantastical, thrilling. <br /><br />Joan Baez singing Dylan's "I Pity the Poor Immigrant" (which borrows from the Scottish "Tramps And Hawkers"):<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gh5QkusIjGc">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gh5Qk...</a><br /><br />P. S. 6/16/17: The Arrival, I say again, silent, is used in K-college classrooms, for which I am very pleased and grateful. It has in the way of the best of "all ages" books some basic simplicity kids of all ages can relate to, and levels of increasing complexity as you get older and more experience in the world (and with comics). Yes, every time you read it you see new things, new levels of metaphor, it's always new, as all great art is. The art is amazing, meticulous and strange and wonderful. It's the source of much conversation and written and artistic response around the world. Do you think you might possibly be moved by a silent story with such creatures? I bet you would be. I am.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16965696222531177748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1674356853" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1674356853" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1674356853?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1674356853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1373558059347857176"><b> <i> "Give me your tired, your poor,<br/>Your huddled masses yearning to breathe free,<br/>The wretched refuse of your teeming shore.<br/>Send these, the homeless, tempest-tost to me,<br/>I lift my lamp beside the golden door!" </i> </b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472835333i/20317750.jpg' alt='arrival 1' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>How did we get from a golden door to prison bars?<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472835333i/20317751.jpg' alt='trump' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Shaun Tan doesn't engage in political polemics. He has no need of words at all. His silent surrealist paintings are more eloquent that all the ghostwriters, TV anchors and political commentators that try to convince us that black is actually whi</span>
  <span id="freeText1373558059347857176" style="display:none"><b> <i> "Give me your tired, your poor,<br>Your huddled masses yearning to breathe free,<br>The wretched refuse of your teeming shore.<br>Send these, the homeless, tempest-tost to me,<br>I lift my lamp beside the golden door!" </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472835333i/20317750.jpg" alt="arrival 1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>How did we get from a golden door to prison bars?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472835333i/20317751.jpg" alt="trump" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Shaun Tan doesn't engage in political polemics. He has no need of words at all. His silent surrealist paintings are more eloquent that all the ghostwriters, TV anchors and political commentators that try to convince us that black is actually white. <b> The Arrival </b> is more than real, because it is Art with a capital A - it is the distillation of the suffering, the alienation, the loneliness and the struggle of countless refugees into a poem without words, a sequence of sepia prints that borrows from Chaplin's silent movies, from Brueghel's fantastic imagination and from Italian neorealism to become more than the sum of its parts: a new medium for a new world, a historical manuscript, a cry for justice and compassion that is as relevant today as it was at the turn of the twentieth century, when the story is set.<br><br>Shaun Tan spent four years working on this album, gathering personal histories from his family, poring over records on Ellis Island, studying faded photographs in museums and interviewing refugee families from all over the world. The resulting album is both familiar and alien, familiar from historical prints that were used as inspiration, and alien in the fantastic elements that are used capture the confusion and the strangeness of being transplanted into a completely new society.<br><br>This is my first contact with the artwork of Shaun Tan, and I find it technically flawless in its use of light, in composition, in the arrangement of panels to describe the passage of time and the sequence of events. Tan uses many techniques from cinematography : tracking shots, wide angle panoramic vistas, fade ins, time-lapse, low angles or bird-eye views, a lot of zooming out from a scene. It's an impressive display of skill that, for me, passed almost unnoticed during the first read through of the album since I was too caught up in the story to pay proper attention. Of course, after I finished I went back to the beginning and went through each panel again at a much slower pace, focusing on details, lighting, facial expressions and so on. I am sure a third or fourth reading will still bring something new to my attention.<br><br>The subject, the silent movie treatment and the fantastic artwork are all good reasons to be generous with my star points, but in the case of "The Arrival" there is also a bit of personal history involved that makes me take the extra step and add it to my favorite shelf. I goes all the way back to 1985, I think, when I used to watch two or three movies a day instead of studying for my exams. And every once in a while, I came out of the darkness of the cinemateque, blinking in the harsh daylight and wondering why is everything still the same way it was before, why is everybody going about their business when something momentous just happened inside, a game changer, a new revelation about myself and about the world. Such is the power of art to define ourselves and to inspire us for change, and Shaun Tan reminded me of one of these movies that I haven't seen in thirty years, yet still shines brightly in my memory. I am talking about "America, America" by Elia Kazan, a comparable masterpiece on the subject of immigration and of the American Dream when seen from outside. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472835333i/20317752._SY540_.jpg" width="400" alt="shaun tan" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1373558059347857176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer985858930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16142860479085353584"><b>Shaun Tan`s Universal Masterpiece</b><br/><br/>Shaun Tan's graphic novel <i>The Arrival</i> tells the story of the refugee experience, depicting its sense of deprivation, danger, loneliness, discovery, and wonder.<br/><br/>Rooted in the picture-story tradition that predates modern comics, the book's wordless language mirrors the protagonist's inability to communicate though words in his new environment; the surreal images provide the story with universal relevance.<br/><br/>Brilliantly conceived and masterfully realized, <i>The Arrival</i> is</span>
  <span id="freeText16142860479085353584" style="display:none"><b>Shaun Tan`s Universal Masterpiece</b><br /><br />Shaun Tan's graphic novel <i>The Arrival</i> tells the story of the refugee experience, depicting its sense of deprivation, danger, loneliness, discovery, and wonder.<br /><br />Rooted in the picture-story tradition that predates modern comics, the book's wordless language mirrors the protagonist's inability to communicate though words in his new environment; the surreal images provide the story with universal relevance.<br /><br />Brilliantly conceived and masterfully realized, <i>The Arrival</i> is the rare case of a graphic novel that can be recommended to just about anyone, regardless of age or cultural background.<br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1592667919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2520752516023741999">Every time I read a graphic with great art I say "THIS IS MY NEW FAVORITE ART STYLE IT'S SO PRETTY" but i'm serious about this one. Probably the most gorgeous book I've ever read. <br/><br/>The Arrival is a story told entirely in pictures about the experience of immigration. It's a surrealistic story, meaning that the world he moves away from and then later into, is very fantastical with sci-fi elements. This was a little bit jarring at first, but once you realize the metaphor that's being established-- t</span>
  <span id="freeText2520752516023741999" style="display:none">Every time I read a graphic with great art I say "THIS IS MY NEW FAVORITE ART STYLE IT'S SO PRETTY" but i'm serious about this one. Probably the most gorgeous book I've ever read. <br /><br />The Arrival is a story told entirely in pictures about the experience of immigration. It's a surrealistic story, meaning that the world he moves away from and then later into, is very fantastical with sci-fi elements. This was a little bit jarring at first, but once you realize the metaphor that's being established-- the foreignness of it all-- then it's really mindboggling. This book provokes so much empathy and sadness, and just the angles of the pictures and the creativity behind it and all the otherworldy elements were so well thought through, it was amazing.<br /><br />Even though there were no words, this really tells a story, and I love that about it. Highly recommend this (even though it's really tall and probably won't fit on your bookshelf lol)</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27813530?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie Stiefvater" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie Stiefvater" href="/user/show/1246837-maggie-stiefvater">Maggie Stiefvater</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who liked The Invention of Hugo Cabret, who like magic realism</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1246837-maggie-stiefvater?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27813530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2445109298240707635">When people recommended <i>The Arrival</i> to me, I thought it would be of academic interest. You know, as an artist, I would find it visually appealing, as a YA author, I would find it stylistically interesting, etc. So it took me a long time to pick it up, and I'm so glad that I did.<br/><br/>The Arrival is a graphic novel (told in illustrations, not in comics) telling the story of an immigrant coming to a new land. The metaphor is brilliant: Shaun Tan sensitively illustrates a very human protagonist coming to</span>
  <span id="freeText2445109298240707635" style="display:none">When people recommended <i>The Arrival</i> to me, I thought it would be of academic interest. You know, as an artist, I would find it visually appealing, as a YA author, I would find it stylistically interesting, etc. So it took me a long time to pick it up, and I'm so glad that I did.<br /><br />The Arrival is a graphic novel (told in illustrations, not in comics) telling the story of an immigrant coming to a new land. The metaphor is brilliant: Shaun Tan sensitively illustrates a very human protagonist coming to a country where everything is literally alien: tentacled fruits, many legged animals, bizarre and fascinating architecture, and bewildering methods of transport. The result is an often laugh-out-loud funny study in magical realism. <br /><br />And my verdict? As someone who makes their living telling their stories with words, I was humbled by just how poignant and humorous and brilliant this book is, without a single word uttered. Highly recommend. And watch out, family, because y'all are getting copies of this for Christmas.<br /><br /><br />***wondering why all my reviews are five stars? Because I'm only reviewing my favorite books -- not every book I read. Consider a novel's presence on my Goodreads bookshelf as a hearty endorsement. I can't believe I just said "hearty." It sounds like a stew.**** </span>
  <a data-text-id="2445109298240707635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2314963909745680180">I'm glad that other people know how to put pictures of the pages of this book into their reviews because if I had that kind of knowledge, I fear my entire review would be page after page of the breathtaking artwork in this wordless graphic novel. That description is so fitting, as this story has no words, yet you read it like you would read a novel. The pencil drawings tell the whole story and a touching, mystical story it is. I believe the author more than achieved what he set out to accomplish</span>
  <span id="freeText2314963909745680180" style="display:none">I'm glad that other people know how to put pictures of the pages of this book into their reviews because if I had that kind of knowledge, I fear my entire review would be page after page of the breathtaking artwork in this wordless graphic novel. That description is so fitting, as this story has no words, yet you read it like you would read a novel. The pencil drawings tell the whole story and a touching, mystical story it is. I believe the author more than achieved what he set out to accomplish when he began the four year(!) process of researching and creating the art and the story. Visually stunning and emotionally affecting, you can <b>feel</b> this! 5 stars.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2593537691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2593537691" />
    <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma"><img alt="PattyMacDotComma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577835191p2/1128612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2593537691?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PattyMacDotComma" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma">PattyMacDotComma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=chcc-library">chcc-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=picture-graphic">picture-graphic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=favourites-kids-ya">favourites-kids-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=kids">kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=ya-new-adult">ya-new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=australian-author">australian-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=fiction-adult">fiction-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=favourites-adult">favourites-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=politics-culture-social">politics-culture-social</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2593537691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3287338424880467676"><b>5★<br/><br/>”The Arrival”</b><br/><br/>That's it - the only text in this extraordinary book. This is a story that needs no translation, art that speaks directly to the “reader”. <br/><br/>The inside front and back covers are completely filled with faces, easily identifiable if you happened to know any of the people (I didn’t) and representing migrants from all over the world, some looking something like you, perhaps. <br/><br/>Tan said that some faces were inspired by the photos from Ellis Island, NY, where so many migrants have entered t</span>
  <span id="freeText3287338424880467676" style="display:none"><b>5★<br><br>”The Arrival”</b><br><br>That's it - the only text in this extraordinary book. This is a story that needs no translation, art that speaks directly to the “reader”. <br><br>The inside front and back covers are completely filled with faces, easily identifiable if you happened to know any of the people (I didn’t) and representing migrants from all over the world, some looking something like you, perhaps. <br><br>Tan said that some faces were inspired by the photos from Ellis Island, NY, where so many migrants have entered the US. He also said that one of the shipboard paintings was based on an 1886 Tom Roberts painting of migrants coming to Australia. <br><br>Some pages are like comic strips, in that they have many pictures divided into rows. It is tempting to glance at the page and move on, but if you do, you will miss the story. Each little painting tells a specific part of the story. Other illustrations may cover a single page or even a double-page spread. They are fantastic!<br><br>I will include a dozen or so illustrations to indicate the way the story is told, but I implore you to find a copy to read yourself. When I asked a daughter who teaches and works with refugee and new migrant children if she’d heard of it, she said quietly and a little condescendingly, “I HAVE it.” <br><br>Say no more. Every school should have this. Every COUNCIL or local government should have this to explain to politicians what is happening in the world.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544507403i/26726622.jpg" width="300" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>There is a deadly but unspecified threat looming over the main character.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726946.jpg" width="300" height="332" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Mother and daughter help Father pack to lead the way to a new life overseas. The family photo is carefully packaged. </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726941.jpg" width="300" height="411" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The decision is made. Mother and Father close the suitcase.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726947.jpg" width="300" height="415" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Father and daughter share a love of paper cranes. The time has come for goodbyes.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726951.jpg" width="300" height="246" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The Arrival, obviously inspired by the Statue of Liberty in New York. </b><br><br>Many of the illustrations are reminiscent of places we’re familiar with, but the specifics are very other-worldly and don’t translate to any particular city or country. There is a section with scenes of a massive jumble of migrants in one place, also inspired, the author says, by Ellis Island. <br><br>Now, Father needs to find a place to stay. He had the foresight to bring a notebook with him, so he sketches a picture of a bed to indicate what he’s looking for.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726949.jpg" width="300" height="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Father is looking for a place to stay in his new country.</b><br><br>Note that the “writing” in the notebook doesn’t correspond to any languages that I’m aware of. We don’t know, or need to know, where this man comes from. He meets a pleasant fellow dressed in a very different costume, who shows him to a room. Note the unusual “pet” in the man’s backpack. This country is certainly very foreign to Father (and me).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726938.jpg" width="300" height="423" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Father remembers his family and admires the picture he’s hung on the wall of his new place.</b><br><br>I don’t know if you can see Father’s little window, or not, but look for the little tail of the pet which is hanging out the window. As I said, this is a very different world.<br><br>He makes a new friend and they begin to share their stories.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726950.jpg" width="300" height="417" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Father sketches what terrified his family in the old country to his new friend, who begins to describe his own story.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726939.jpg" width="300" height="409" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>An illustration of the terror that faced Father’s new friend.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726943.jpg" width="300" height="414" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>This is how the new friend and his family hid and escaped their oppressors.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726942.jpg" width="300" height="427" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Father enjoys a happy meal with his new friend’s family, including the pets.</b><br><br>The pets seem to be a kind of dog and cat, but the food is reminiscent only of eggplant and various squashes, I think. Not that there’s anything wrong with them!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726944.jpg" width="300" height="424" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>An evening with friends! Music, pets, folding paper animals, a bowl for Father.</b><br><br>Here I will fast-forward. We have seen Father try a few jobs, one with difficulty because he doesn’t know the language and hangs posters upside down (how’s YOUR Chinese, eh?).<br><br>But he’s saved up money, sent it home, and waits for his wife and daughter. They are “flying” in. Their transport is something like a Dr. Who phonebox hanging from a balloon.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726940.jpg" width="300" height="434" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>They’re coming, they’re coming! Father runs to meet them.</b><br><br>After they arrive, they sit down for a happy family meal.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726945.jpg" width="300" height="435" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Dinner “at home” with the family photo on the wall and the new pet at the table.</b><br><br>Later, the little girl takes the “dog” for a walk around her new neighbourhood and finds an even more recent arrival trying to figure out where she is.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726948.jpg" width="300" height="406" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The daughter helps a young woman read her map.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544514550i/26726937.jpg" width="300" height="424" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The new migrant has a suitcase much like Father’s, and the daughter shows her where she wants to go.</b><br><br>Full circle. What goes around, comes around. This is the most beautiful book. It’s all in muted sepia tones, giving it a very old look, which helps identify it as an old story. There are no colours to make you think of any particular country.<br><br>People fleeing oppression, terror, war, and abject poverty deserve a chance. I wish everyone could read this and understand that this "old" story is actually current. I also wish it were possible to drop politicians into completely foreign environments with no money or language, just to see what it's like.<br><br>Find a copy! You'll want to own one. It's 132 pages, large format.<br><br>P.S. Many of the images are online if you google the title, author, and images. There is also a beautiful, 14-minute video version posted several years ago that teachers are using in classes. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://vimeo.com/74292820">https://vimeo.com/74292820</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3287338424880467676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1931937167" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1931937167" />
    <a title="Trudie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4617856-trudie"><img alt="Trudie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586207854p2/4617856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1931937167?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trudie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trudie" href="/user/show/4617856-trudie">Trudie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617856-trudie?shelf=australia">australia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617856-trudie?shelf=graphic-novel-comic">graphic-novel-comic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617856-trudie?shelf=pictorial">pictorial</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617856-trudie?shelf=art">art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617856-trudie?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617856-trudie?shelf=best-of-2017">best-of-2017</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1931937167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3181784887564053094">In my ongoing effort to tackle some of my more "pictorial" books I decided to spend a few days absorbing the majestic work of Australian artist / illustrator Shaun Tan. <i> The Arrival </i> is surely his Magnum Opus, a four year project resulting in this stunning sepia toned homage to the migrant experience. <br/>The artwork is meticulous in this, the colour palette morphing from warm, rich sepia tones, to greys and blacks, matching the changing tone of the story. The world drawn here is one almost entirely</span>
  <span id="freeText3181784887564053094" style="display:none">In my ongoing effort to tackle some of my more "pictorial" books I decided to spend a few days absorbing the majestic work of Australian artist / illustrator Shaun Tan. <i> The Arrival </i> is surely his Magnum Opus, a four year project resulting in this stunning sepia toned homage to the migrant experience. <br />The artwork is meticulous in this, the colour palette morphing from warm, rich sepia tones, to greys and blacks, matching the changing tone of the story. The world drawn here is one almost entirely fantastical, yet the historical influences on this story are hard to miss, imagery from Ellis Island, steamships carrying refugees, scenes of war and chaos - are all mixed in with the strange language and animals of this fantasy land. It is brilliantly done, making the "reader" feel as mystified by this new world as the protagonist of the story. These feelings of empathy are something the world desperately needs more of. <br /><br />A "silent novel" masterpiece. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3181784887564053094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_153945665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153945665" />
    <a title="TK421" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2624672-tk421"><img alt="TK421" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327476609p2/2624672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153945665?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TK421" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TK421" href="/user/show/2624672-tk421">TK421</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2624672-tk421?shelf=graphic-novels-comics">graphic-novels-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153945665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15213678512140602156">I never expected to like this picture book. In fact, I don't like many picture books. I have no problem making up a story for the pictures; I just like it more when a story is provided. But when I opened up THE ARRIVAL, I instantly knew there was something different about this book. <br/><br/>This is the story of what I can only imagine is the way millions of European immigrants felt as they left their homelands and ventured forth to become part of America. <br/><br/>With each page, I thought of my grandfather, Hil</span>
  <span id="freeText15213678512140602156" style="display:none">I never expected to like this picture book. In fact, I don't like many picture books. I have no problem making up a story for the pictures; I just like it more when a story is provided. But when I opened up THE ARRIVAL, I instantly knew there was something different about this book. <br /><br />This is the story of what I can only imagine is the way millions of European immigrants felt as they left their homelands and ventured forth to become part of America. <br /><br />With each page, I thought of my grandfather, Hiljo Ranko. He came from Holland with his brothers in 1908. He was the only one of them that knew any English. I think he must have felt as if he had entered into a completely New World, filled with new sounds and sights. Shaun Tan illustrates these feelings amazingly through his adroit depictions of surreal creatures and shapes that take form on each page. <br /><br />My brothers and I are only the second generation of boys from my father's family born here in America. I've never known what it feels like to say goodbye to a life I was once lived. I've never known what frights linger around corners in a country that has habitually scorned one set of immigrants after another. THE ARRIVAL put all this into perspective for me. For a time, as I looked at the pages, I could feel what my grandfather had felt: sadness, excitement, triumph. For a time, I became my grandfather. As schmaltzy as that sounds, that is the only way I can adequately describe what this book did to me. <br /><br />Take the time to seek out this book. Look at the pages and study the images. I'm pretty sure I will not be alone in thinking how amazing our ancestor's stories are.<br /><br />HIGHLY RECCOMENDED<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15213678512140602156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_495642638" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/495642638" />
    <a title="Forrest" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/811928-forrest"><img alt="Forrest" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558621304p2/811928.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/495642638?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Forrest" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Forrest" href="/user/show/811928-forrest">Forrest</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer495642638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13855346562214384607">A surprisingly moving story about hope and yearning in the context of immigration. The lack of words really forces the "reader" to try to apprehend what is happening without any understanding of the full intent or meaning behind the characters' body language. Of course, this puts the "reader" in the position of the main character, an immigrant who cannot understand the language of his new homeland and is unfamiliar with its customs. This creates a funny kind of reverse-metafiction that effective</span>
  <span id="freeText13855346562214384607" style="display:none">A surprisingly moving story about hope and yearning in the context of immigration. The lack of words really forces the "reader" to try to apprehend what is happening without any understanding of the full intent or meaning behind the characters' body language. Of course, this puts the "reader" in the position of the main character, an immigrant who cannot understand the language of his new homeland and is unfamiliar with its customs. This creates a funny kind of reverse-metafiction that effectively puts the audience right in the middle of the story's emotional "space". Tan's customary baroque weirdness is on display as we "hear" the stories of several immigrants who encounter each other and tell their tales of how they arrived in this strange land, but Tan shows a greater restraint here than he does in <a href="http://forrestaguirre.blogspot.com/2012/09/lost-and-found-three-by-shaun-tan.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Lost and Found</a>. I prefer the outrageously imaginative art of <i>Lost and Found</i> to the sepia tone nostalgia of <i>The Arrival</i>, though the latter book does carry more emotional impact.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13855346562214384607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2935972568" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2935972568" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2935972568?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780734415868" href="/book/show/23399671-the-arrival">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Trish by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/36890366-sud666">Sud666</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2935972568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6413559195861347578">I found this after a friend recommended it to me. <br/><br/>It‘s the story of a man leaving his country (and family) behind as there are monsters there. He embarks on a journey across the ocean, landing in a fantasy-version of NYC. There, he has to find his bearings, meets all kinds of people, manages to find work to ultimately send money back home that will bring his wife and daughter to him.<br/><br/>What makes this story special is that it is told in graphics only. The entire book only shows pictures, no text - </span>
  <span id="freeText6413559195861347578" style="display:none">I found this after a friend recommended it to me. <br><br>It‘s the story of a man leaving his country (and family) behind as there are monsters there. He embarks on a journey across the ocean, landing in a fantasy-version of NYC. There, he has to find his bearings, meets all kinds of people, manages to find work to ultimately send money back home that will bring his wife and daughter to him.<br><br>What makes this story special is that it is told in graphics only. The entire book only shows pictures, no text - but the illustrations (graphites) are gorgeous! They are all in sepia, sometimes darker, sometimes brighter, showing in incredible detail how strange yet wonderful this distant new land is.<br>We have fantasy creatures living side-by-side with the humans, the evil forces of oppression and war depicted as dragons and giant monsters.<br><br>The reader thus learns of the desperation of immigrants, of their alienation at simple things like food they‘ve never seen before, of the difficulty due to them not speaking the language at first - but the reader also learns of perseverance, hope and the immigrants working hard to make a new life.<br><br>A remarkable story that emphazises a very important topic - no, it‘s not timely as immigration is a very old subject, only being treated as if it was a new problem. As usual, both sides have to be looked at in order to obtain an informed opinion and most countries have benfitted from immigration workers throughout history (we‘re talking about the kind of immigrants that are grateful for a new chance, that want to learn the language and contribute in their new home).<br><br>Personally, more than the topic itself, I‘m still in awe of the book‘s design and Shaun Tan‘s illustrations that tell the story vividly without any words - no wonder this book won several awards.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567253797i/28079384.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="6413559195861347578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1782560552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8835159379847371674">OH MY GOD!!!!!! This is one of the best books I have ever read! Can I have some more stars to put?! <br/><br/>‘The Arrival’ is a book without words, a silent book! It has pictures, only pictures and they are mesmerizing! The writer and illustrator, Shaun Tan has done an amazing job. Hats off! His way of conveying emotions of the story to the reader only using pictures is totally out of the world! <br/><br/>It is a story of a man who leaves his country to find a better place for his family and ends up in a new place</span>
  <span id="freeText8835159379847371674" style="display:none">OH MY GOD!!!!!! This is one of the best books I have ever read! Can I have some more stars to put?! <br /><br />‘The Arrival’ is a book without words, a silent book! It has pictures, only pictures and they are mesmerizing! The writer and illustrator, Shaun Tan has done an amazing job. Hats off! His way of conveying emotions of the story to the reader only using pictures is totally out of the world! <br /><br />It is a story of a man who leaves his country to find a better place for his family and ends up in a new place where things are pretty weird! But gradually he gets used to these peculiar things and leads his life like a normal citizen of the town. <br />Basically it’s a story of immigrant people who face tons of problems in a new country. <br /><br />The departure of the man leaving his family behind was heartbreaking. But the ending just melted my heart! I wanted few more pages of it! Such a beautiful book. <br /><br />I have read the pdf version for now. But someday I’ll definitely collect a copy of it. &lt;3 <br /><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7ubcsAo/4zWaEODwt/V6jTk04VNQ/V74zUau44O5snBqdZTRqe+QD2BZk7lZ5k9So7FxmJnJZNXd5G+wBCu4GQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('n/yKlrR0Jf5DGE1DC+Tav5145ZxSPPq08ROgYjkLIiMbb8L3F6RWxLlRPgrl9+9gB/11V5sIwJnhsWExvpkoSg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer16173155269670152433"><i>Shaun Tan</i> (born 1974) is the illustrator and author of award-winning children's books. After freelancing for some years from a studio at Mt. Lawley, Tan relocated to Melbourne, Victoria in 2007. Tan was the Illustrator in Residence at the University of Melbourne's Department of Language Literacy and Arts Education for two weeks through an annual Fellowship offered by the May Gibbs Children’s Liter</span>
  <span id="freeText16173155269670152433" style="display:none"><i>Shaun Tan</i> (born 1974) is the illustrator and author of award-winning children's books. After freelancing for some years from a studio at Mt. Lawley, Tan relocated to Melbourne, Victoria in 2007. Tan was the Illustrator in Residence at the University of Melbourne's Department of Language Literacy and Arts Education for two weeks through an annual Fellowship offered by the May Gibbs Children’s Literature Trust. 2009 World Fantasy Award for Best Artist.<br />2011 he won his first Oscar in the Category <i>Best Short Animated Film</i> for his work <i>The Lost Thing</i></span>
